## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics ODEs. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are single-species rate laws where the reaction rate depends on A (reaction order, saturation/inhibition) and/or explicitly on time (changing conditions, catalyst deactivation, programmed forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface/photochemical kinetics where rate is independent of A over a range)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (elementary unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- First-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward steady state concentration c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order behavior)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate law with reaction order c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating production with limiting depletion/capacity c1)
- Saturation-limited consumption (Monod-like in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to limited active sites/catalyst)
- Inhibition/feedback (decreasing effective rate at high A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A**c2) (self-inhibition or crowding/viscosity effects)
- Time-varying first-order (rate ramp-up): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (increasing rate coefficient due to heating/activation over time)
- Time-varying first-order (deactivation/aging): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or reagent exhaustion reducing rate)
- Sum of baseline + transient rate coefficient: dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) (fast initial contribution that decays to a baseline rate)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodic illumination/mixing/temperature oscillations modulating rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is nearly constant (independent of A), a zero-order term (-c0) is indicated; A(t) tends to be approximately linear until depletion.
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line in dA_dt vs A through the origin), first-order kinetics (-c0*A) is likely; A(t) tends to be exponential.
- If dA_dt changes sign around a nonzero concentration, include a steady-state/equilibrium form -c0*(A - c1), implying relaxation toward A = c1.
- Curvature consistent with faster-than-linear decay (|dA_dt| rising steeply with A) suggests higher-order or power-law dependence -c0*A**c1 with c1 > 1.
- A rate that increases at low A then levels off at high A suggests saturation rational forms like -c0*A/(A + c1).
- Self-accelerating behavior (slow start, then faster change) can be captured by autocatalytic terms like c0*A*(c1 - A) or positive A-dependent production minus depletion.
- Systematic drift of apparent rate constant over time (even at similar A) suggests explicit time dependence via exp(±c*t) or additive transient terms in the coefficient of A.
- Periodic ripples in dA_dt vs t at similar A suggest forcing terms like sin(c*t) multiplying the kinetic rate coefficient.

Variable roles: t appears only inside exponentials (fast exp(c1·t) with c1≈−61.4 and slow exp(c4·t) with c4≈−0.078), while A enters both as A and |A|^(1/3), all scaled and modulated by the same denominator that also depends on exp(c1·t). With c1 very negative, exp(c1·t) collapses to ~0 for t>0 so the expression is ≈ A·c3·exp(c4·t) + c6·|A|^(1/3) (since c0,c5 multiply vanishing exp(c1·t)), whereas for sufficiently negative t where exp(c1·t) is huge the denominator ≈ c2·exp(c1·t) and the terms involving exp(c1·t) saturate to constants ≈ A·(c0/c2) + |A|^(1/3)·(c5/c2) while the A·c3·exp(c4·t) term is strongly suppressed by 1/exp(c1·t). Numerically, c6=0.208 is the dominant |A|^(1/3) coefficient, c3=−0.675 sets the main t-varying A-term for t>0, and the small c0=−0.039 and c5=0.0176 contributions matter mainly only in the negative-t saturation regime via division by the small c2=0.0465.
Fitted params       : c0=-3.9305e-02, c1=-6.1396e+01, c2=4.6541e-02, c3=-6.7505e-01, c4=-7.8313e-02, c5=1.7590e-02, c6=2.0847e-01
Train NMSE          : 4.09e-15
Test NMSE           : 4.17e-15
OOD Test NMSE       : 5.63e-13

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK17)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_f*A**c3
Candidate formulas: 64

GT is the fixed function
\[
F(t,A)=0.2084703204063362\,A^{1/3}-0.6750544468008356\,A\,e^{-0.0783132263146032\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be expressible as “(constant)\(\cdot A^{1/3}\)” plus “(constant)\(\cdot A e^{k t}\)” with \(k=-0.0783132263\), and with no extra \(A\)-powers, no denominators depending on \(t\) or \(A\), and no extra additive constants. Also, under the relaxed domain \(A\ge 0\), \(\lvert A\rvert=A\) and \(\lvert A\rvert^{1/3}=A^{1/3}\).

Below, for each candidate I check whether we can choose its free constants to reduce exactly to the GT form.

---

### 1.
Has a common denominator \((c2 e^{c1 t}+1)\). GT has no such denominator. Only way to remove it is make it constant: would require \(c2=0\), giving denominator \(1\). Then expression becomes
\[
A c0 e^{c1 t}+A c3 e^{c4 t}+c5 e^{c1 t}A^{1/3}+c6 A^{1/3},
\]
which has potentially two different exponentials and an \(A^{1/3}e^{c1 t}\) term not in GT. You can zero some coefficients, but you still can’t simultaneously get exactly one \(A e^{kt}\) term and one plain \(A^{1/3}\) term unless you set \(c3=0,c5=0\) and match \(c1\) to \(k\). Then it becomes \(A c0 e^{k t}+c6 A^{1/3}\), which *could* match GT by choosing \(c0=-0.675054...\), \(c6=0.208470...\), \(c1=k\). However note: with \(c2=0\) we already removed denominator; that is allowed. So **candidate 1 can match**.

### 2.
\[
c0 A^{1/3}+ c1 A e^{c2 t}
\]
Exactly the GT structure. Choose \(c0=0.2084703204063362\), \(c1=-0.6750544468008356\), \(c2=-0.0783132263146032\). **Matches.**

### 3.
\[
A c0 e^{c1 t}+ c2 |A|^{1/3}
\]
With \(A\ge 0\), \(|A|^{1/3}=A^{1/3}\). Choose \(c0=-0.6750544468008356\), \(c1=-0.0783132263146032\), \(c2=0.2084703204063362\). **Matches.**

### 4.
\[
c0 e^{c1 t}|A| + c2 |A|^{1/3}
\]
With \(A\ge 0\), \(|A|=A\). Same as candidate 3. Choose constants as above. **Matches.**

### 5.
Has denominator \((\sqrt A + c1)\). GT has none. To remove dependence on \(A\), would need \(\sqrt A + c1\) constant, impossible for variable \(A\). No way. **No match.**

### 6.
Contains rational terms with denominator \((A^{c1}+c2)\) plus an extra separate \(A^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\) term. To match GT (no denominator), would need denominator constant: impossible unless \(c1=0\) so \(A^{c1}=1\), then denominator \(1+c2\) constant. That’s possible. Then first two terms become linear combinations of \(A\) and \(A^{c3}e^{c5 t}\) with a constant scaling. But GT needs \(A e^{kt}\) (not plain \(A\)) and \(A^{1/3}\) (not multiplied by an exponential). You could set the first term to 0, use second term to produce \(A e^{kt}\) by setting \(c3=1\), and use third term to produce \(A^{1/3}\) by setting \(c6=1/3\) and \(c8=0\) (so \(e^{0t}=1\)). However the third term is \(A^{1/3}c7\) only if \(c8=0\). This seems feasible, but check: second term is \(\frac{A^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}}{1+c2}\). Set \(c3=1\), \(c5=k\), \(c4/(1+c2)=-0.675054...\). Third term set \(c6=1/3\), \(c8=0\), \(c7=0.208470...\). First term set \(c0=0\). This yields exactly GT. **Matches.**

### 7.
\[
A c0 e^{c1 t}+ c3 A^{c2}+ c5 A^{c4}
\]
GT needs one \(A e^{kt}\) and one \(A^{1/3}\). Set \(c0=-0.675054...\), \(c1=k\). Make one power term be \(A^{1/3}\): set \(c2=1/3\), \(c3=0.208470...\). Kill the other power term by setting \(c5=0\). **Matches.**

### 8.
Same as 3 but with extra constant \(c3\). Set \(c3=0\) and match as in 3. **Matches.**

### 9.
\[
A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + c3 e^{c4 t}|A|^{c5}
\]
GT has no plain \(A\) term, so set \(c0=0\). Need \(A e^{kt}\): set \(c1=-0.675054...\), \(c2=k\). Need \(A^{1/3}\) with no exponential: set \(c4=0\) so \(e^{0t}=1\), \(c5=1/3\), \(c3=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 10.
Has cosine factor in the third term. To match GT, we’d need that cosine term to be identically 1 (or absorbable). You can set \(c5=0\) so \(\cos(0)=1\), and set \(c4=0\) to remove exponential, and \(c6=1/3\). Also set \(c0=0\) to remove plain \(A\). Then second term matches \(A e^{kt}\). Works. **Matches.**

### 11.
Only has \(A\) terms and one power term \(A^{c5}\), no exponential in \(t\). Cannot produce \(A e^{kt}\) with \(k\neq 0\). **No match.**

### 12.
Same issue: has \(A\) terms and \(A^{c6}\) but no \(t\)-exponential multiplying \(A\). Cannot match \(A e^{kt}\). **No match.**

### 13.
\[
A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + c4 A^{c3}
\]
Set \(c0=0\). Set \(c1=-0.675054...\), \(c2=k\). Set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 14.
Has denominator \((A^{c1}+c2)\) and extra affine-in-\(t\) term \(c6 t+c7\). Even if denominator made constant via \(c1=0\), you still must kill \(c6 t+c7\) by \(c6=0,c7=0\). Then you can match similarly to candidate 6 by using the exponential term for \(A e^{kt}\) and the other term for \(A^{1/3}\) (but note both are divided by same constant). Feasible: set \(c1=0\), choose \(c0=0\), set \(c3=1\), \(c5=k\), and scale \(c4/(1+c2)=-0.675054...\). But then where does \(A^{1/3}\) come from? First term is \(A c0/(1+c2)\) (linear), not \(A^{1/3}\). So cannot. **No match.**

### 15.
Similar rational structure plus \(c6 e^{A c7}\) (depends on \(A\) exponentially), which GT doesn’t have. Only removable by \(c6=0\). Then same problem as 14: remaining terms can’t yield \(A^{1/3}\) because the non-exponential term is linear in \(A\). **No match.**

### 16.
\[
\frac{A^5 c0 e^{c1 t}}{A^4+c2}+\frac{A^{c3}c4}{A^4+c2}
\]
Denominator depends on \(A\) (unless impossible \(A^4+c2\) constant). No match. **No match.**

### 17.
Like 1 but with extra \(e^{c2 t}\) factors and denominator \((c3 e^{c1 t}+1)\). Set \(c3=0\) to remove denominator. Then you can zero unwanted terms and choose one \(A e^{kt}\) and one \(A^{1/3}\) (set the \(A^{1/3}\) exponential coefficient to 0). Works similarly to 1. **Matches.**

### 18.
Has extra rational term \(A c3/(A^{c4}+c5)\) which cannot become \(A^{1/3}\) without leaving denominator dependence on \(A\). You can set \(c3=0\) to remove it, leaving \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\), which lacks \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 19.
Rational terms plus an added \(A^{c3}c4\) (no \(t\)). If set \(c1=0\) to make denominator constant, you can use the rational exponential term for \(A e^{kt}\) (set \(c5=1\), \(c7=k\)) and use \(A^{c3}c4\) for \(A^{1/3}\) (set \(c3=1/3\)). Set the remaining rational non-exponential term to 0 via \(c0=0\). **Matches.**

### 20.
Contains an extra \(A c3 e^{c4 t}\) term outside the denominator. You can set \(c3=0\). Then it reduces to a form like 19 but without the standalone \(A^{1/3}\) unless you use the first rational term—yet that term is linear in \(A\). If denominator constant (via \(c1=0\)), first term is linear \(A\), not \(A^{1/3}\). So cannot. **No match.**

### 21.
Has \(A c3\) and constant \(c7\). Set them 0. Remaining is rational with denominator \((A^{c1}+c2)\). If make denominator constant via \(c1=0\), then you have linear \(A\) plus \(A^{c4}e^{c6 t}\). You can make the exponential term be \(A e^{kt}\) (set \(c4=1,c6=k\)), but then no \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 22.
Extra \(c6\log(A c7+1)\) cannot be in GT unless \(c6=0\). Then same structure as 21/14: cannot get \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 23.
Has \(A^2 c0\) etc; hard to remove all extra structures and get exactly two terms. Even setting many coefficients 0, the remaining rational pieces are linear in \(A\) over \((A^{c2}+c3)\), not \(A^{1/3}\) without denominator dependence. **No match.**

### 24.
Has extra \(c3 e^{c4 t}\) and extra power term and constant. You can set those extra coefficients to 0, leaving \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\), missing \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 25.
Has sine term; can set its coefficient \(c6=0\) and also set extra \(A\) terms to 0, but then no \(A^{1/3}\) unless \(A^{c5}\) term remains—yet it’s inside the sine product. Not workable. **No match.**

### 26.
Second and third terms are \(A^{c1+c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) and \(A^{c3}c6 e^{c5 t}\) (both share same exponential), plus a rational linear term. Hard to get one exponential \(A e^{kt}\) and one non-exponential \(A^{1/3}\). If set \(c5=0\) to make non-exponential, then you lose required \(t\)-dependence. If keep \(c5=k\), both power terms carry \(e^{kt}\), but GT’s \(A^{1/3}\) term has no \(t\). **No match.**

### 27.
Denominator \(A^4+c2\) depends on \(A\). No match. **No match.**

### 28.
Extra \(e^{c7 t}\log(Ac8+1)\) term; must set \(c6=0\). Then reduces to rational form like 14/21, still can’t produce \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 29.
Has extra \(A c3\) and \(A c4 e^{c5 t}\) outside denominator. You can set those to 0, leaving rational terms; again cannot produce \(A^{1/3}\) without denominator dependence. **No match.**

### 30.
All terms share denominator \((A^{c1}+c2)\). If make denominator constant via \(c1=0\), first term becomes \(c0 A^{1/3}/(1+c2)\) good, but the exponential terms become linear in \(A\) times \(e^{c4 t}\) (good for \(A e^{kt}\)) plus also a linear non-exponential term \(A c5/(1+c2)\) which must be killed by \(c5=0\). Then choose \(c4=k\) and set combined coefficient of \(A e^{kt}\) appropriately by choosing \(c3,c6\). Works. **Matches.**

### 31.
Has a logistic-type denominator in \(t\) for the \(A\) and \(A^{1/3}\) terms, plus a separate \(A^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) term. To match GT, easiest is set \(c1=0\) so denominator is 1. Then expression becomes
\[
A c0 + A^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t} + c6 e^{c2 t}A^{1/3}+c7 A^{1/3}.
\]
Need no plain \(A\): set \(c0=0\). Need no \(A^{1/3}\) exponential: set \(c6=0\). Then set \(c3=1\), \(c4=-0.675054...\), \(c5=k\), and \(c7=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 32.
Extra \(c6\log(c7 t+1)\) must be 0; then remaining rational form cannot give \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 33.
Extra \(c6 e^{c7 t}\) must be 0; then remaining rational form cannot give \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 34.
Has extra sine-in-\(A\) and log-in-\(t\) terms; can set their coefficients to 0, leaving \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}c4\). Then set \(c0=0\), \(c1=-0.675054...\), \(c2=k\), \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 35.
No way to reduce to exactly \(A^{1/3}\) plus \(A e^{kt}\) because structures are \(A^2\) and rational-in-\(A\) with same denominator. **No match.**

### 36.
Set \(c1=0\) to remove denominator. Then becomes \(A c0 + A c3 e^{c4 t} + c5 e^{c2 t}A^{1/3}+c6 A^{1/3}\). Set \(c0=0\), set \(c5=0\), set \(c3=-0.675054...\), \(c4=k\), set \(c6=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 37.
Has extra \(A c3/(A+c4)\) term; can set \(c3=0\). Remaining rational terms still can’t yield \(A^{1/3}\) (same issue). **No match.**

### 38.
Set logistic denominator off via \(c1=0\). Then \(A c0 + A c3 + A c4 e^{c5 t} + c6 e^{c2 t}A^{1/3}+c7 A^{1/3}\). Kill plain \(A\) terms by \(c0=0,c3=0\). Kill \(A^{1/3}\) exponential by \(c6=0\). Set \(c4=-0.675054...\), \(c5=k\), \(c7=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 39.
Pure rational form with shared denominator; cannot produce \(A^{1/3}\) unless denominator constant and one numerator is \(A^{1/3}\), but numerators are \(A\) and \(A^{c3}e^{c5 t}\). If denominator constant (set \(c1=0\)), first term is linear \(A\), second is exponential-in-\(t\) times \(A^{c3}\). You can set \(c3=1/3\) to get \(A^{1/3}e^{c5 t}\) but GT’s \(A^{1/3}\) has no \(t\). If set \(c5=0\), then you lose the needed \(t\)-dependence for the \(A\) term. **No match.**

### 40.
Extra rational-in-\(A\) terms in \(t\) and constant; cannot be removed to exactly GT unless coefficients 0, reducing to candidate 39 which already fails. **No match.**

### 41.
Has extra \(A c3\) outside denominator; can set \(c3=0\), leaving candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 42.
Has extra \(A c3(c4+t)^{c5}\); set \(c3=0\), leaving candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 43.
\[
A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t} + c6\log(c7 t+1)
\]
Set \(c6=0\). Need only one exponential term in \(A\): set \(c0=0\). Then choose \(A c1 e^{c2 t}\) as the \(A e^{kt}\) term: \(c1=-0.675054...\), \(c2=k\). Choose the power term to be \(A^{1/3}\) with no exponential: set \(c3=1/3\), \(c5=0\), \(c4=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 44.
Has \(c3|A|^{c4}\) and log term. Set log coefficient \(c5=0\). Then expression is \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + c3 A^{c4}\) (for \(A\ge0\)). Set \(c0=0\), \(c1=-0.675054...\), \(c2=k\), \(c4=1/3\), \(c3=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 45.
Same as 44 but without Abs; set log coefficient 0 and match similarly. **Matches.**

### 46.
Rational form plus constant. Set constant \(c6=0\). Remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 47.
All terms share denominator \((A^{c0}+c3)\) and are proportional to \(A e^{c2 t}\) or \(A\). No \(A^{1/3}\) term possible without denominator dependence. **No match.**

### 48.
Has log-of-\(A\) term; must set \(c4=0\). Then becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3\), no \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 49.
Extra rational-in-\(t\) terms; can set \(c6=0,c9=0\), leaving candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 50.
Denominator \(\sqrt A + c1\) depends on \(A\); cannot match GT. **No match.**

### 51.
Extra \(\log(c7 e^{A c8 + c9 t}+1)\) term; must set \(c6=0\). Remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 52.
\[
A c0 e^{c1 t} + \frac{c2 e^{c3 t}A^{1/3}}{c4 e^{c3 t}+1} + \frac{c5 A^{1/3}}{c4 e^{c3 t}+1}
\]
To make the \(A^{1/3}\) part independent of \(t\), set \(c4=0\) so denominator is 1, and set \(c2=0\) to remove \(e^{c3 t}\) factor. Then it becomes \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c5 A^{1/3}\). Choose \(c0=-0.675054...\), \(c1=k\), \(c5=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 53.
Second term is \(A^{c3+c4} c5 e^{c6 t}\) (no denominator), first is rational \(A c0/(A^{c1}+c2)\). Hard to get both GT terms: you can make second term be \(A e^{kt}\) (set \(c3+c4=1\), \(c6=k\)), but then no \(A^{1/3}\) unless first term becomes \(A^{1/3}\), which it cannot without \(A\)-dependent denominator. **No match.**

### 54.
\[
A c0/(A^{c1}+c2) + c4 A^{c3} e^{c5 t}
\]
Second term could be \(A e^{kt}\) (set \(c3=1,c5=k\)), but first term cannot become \(A^{1/3}\) without denominator dependence. If make denominator constant via \(c1=0\), first term is linear \(A\), not \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 55.
\[
A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + \frac{c3 e^{c2 t}A^{1/3}}{c4 e^{c2 t}+1} + \frac{c5 A^{1/3}}{c4 e^{c2 t}+1}
\]
Set \(c0=0\). To remove \(t\)-dependence from the \(A^{1/3}\) part, set \(c4=0\) (denominator 1) and set \(c3=0\). Then get \(A c1 e^{c2 t} + c5 A^{1/3}\). Choose \(c1=-0.675054...\), \(c2=k\), \(c5=0.208470...\). **Matches.**

### 56.
\[
A\cdot A^{c0} c1 + \frac{A^{c2}c3 e^{c4 t}}{A^{c5}+c6}
\]
First term is \(c1 A^{c0+1}\) (no \(t\)). Could set \(c0=-2/3\) to make \(A^{1/3}\). Second term would need to be \(A e^{kt}\) with no denominator dependence; but denominator depends on \(A\) unless \(c5=0\) making it constant. If \(c5=0\), denominator constant, then choose \(c2=1\), \(c4=k\). Then yes: first term gives \(A^{1/3}\), second gives \(A e^{kt}\). **Matches.**

### 57.
Extra \(c6 t^{c7}\) must be 0; then remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 58.
Extra \(c6 t (A+c7)^{c8}\) must be 0; then remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 59.
Extra \(\sin(Ac7+c8)\) must be 0; then remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 60.
Has extra \(A c3\) and \(A c4\sin(\cdot)\); can set \(c3=0,c4=0\), leaving rational form like 41 which fails to produce \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 61.
Extra \(\sin(c7 t+c8)\) must be 0; then remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 62.
Extra \(A^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\cos(c9 t)\) must be 0; then remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 63.
Extra \(A^{c6}c7\sin(c8 t+c9)\) must be 0; then remaining is candidate 39 form which fails. **No match.**

### 64.
Has extra \(c4\log(c5 A^{1/3}+1)\); must set \(c4=0\). Then becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3\), no \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**
